# Comments for Question 1, LLM=Mistral Large 2

== Grader: Claude 3.7 Sonnet ==
  * grade_story_100.txt (grade=6.2)
    Eli's character as a "vivid dreamer" and "rationally mischievous" is established but not deeply explored. His motivation to unravel cosmic deceptions is present but lacks specificity. The pressed penny collection connects well to his character, but his emotional journey feels somewhat rushed rather than organically developed. The revelation at the end feels more told than earned through character growth.

  * grade_story_101.txt (grade=5.2)
    Edmund's character has a promising foundation with his "cryptically obvious sadness," but his motivation lacks specificity. While we understand he designs rooms to heal others, his personal stakes remain vague. The connection between his weathered heart and his actions needs deeper exploration. His reaction to the bee pin feels somewhat mechanical rather than revealing significant character depth.

  * grade_story_102.txt (grade=5.2)
    Silas's character development from spineless mercenary to courageous explorer has a clear arc, but feels rushed and relies too heavily on telling rather than showing. His transformation lacks psychological depth and specific moments that convincingly demonstrate his growth. The initial characterization of his spinelessness is established but not deeply explored through concrete examples or internal conflict.

  * grade_story_10.txt (grade=5.2)
    The character's fatal flaws (temper and pride) are established but not demonstrated through action. Elias's transformation feels told rather than shown, with his motivation for forgiveness appearing abruptly rather than emerging organically. His "precisely innovative" swordsmanship is merely stated without meaningful integration into his character development.

  * grade_story_0.txt (grade=5.2)
    Edmund's character is somewhat developed through his sheepish nature and analytical abilities, but remains superficial. His motivation to "unite people" feels underdeveloped and stated rather than demonstrated. The character lacks depth beyond his function in the plot, with minimal emotional complexity or internal conflict. His personality doesn't evolve meaningfully through the story.

  * grade_story_1.txt (grade=5.2)
    Edgar's phobia-ridden nature is established but insufficiently explored. His motivation to "dance on the edge of madness" feels more like a metaphor than a driving force. The character lacks specificity—we never learn which phobias plague him or how being a stunt double shapes his worldview. His transformation feels too abrupt and unearned, with little concrete evidence of his internal struggle beyond vague statements about "trembling hands."

  * grade_story_105.txt (grade=6.8)
    Edmund's character has clear motivation and the "strangely trustworthy" attribute creates an interesting tension with his trespassing. His connection to the seashell reveals vulnerability. However, his scholarly nature feels underdeveloped beyond surface description, and his immediate calm when confronting the witch seems inconsistent with his earlier "wild and eager" demeanor.

  * grade_story_106.txt (grade=6.2)
    Eamon's character has a clear motivation and his sullenness is well-established through his isolation and yearning. His bias against technology creates an interesting contradiction given his environment. However, his transformation feels somewhat abrupt and his personality lacks nuance—we're told more about his situation than shown his unique voice or complex emotional landscape.

  * grade_story_108.txt (grade=5.2)
    Edgar Harper shows some development through his realization about responsibility, but his initial motivation feels underdeveloped. The character lacks depth beyond serving as a vehicle for the plot.

  * grade_story_104.txt (grade=6.2)

His reaction to finding the package shows a glimpse of complexity, but his character development remains limited within the word count.

  * grade_story_107.txt (grade=4.2)

The transformation feels rushed and unearned, telling us about Harold's redemption rather than showing his internal struggle.

  * grade_story_109.txt (grade=6.2)
